import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl

OP_TYPE = "softmax"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hard-coded tuning for the five benchmark shapes.  The benchmark creates
# a fresh Model(*init_args) per shape, so we can safely specialise.
# Fallback heuristics handle unseen sizes.
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
_KERNEL_CFG = {
    (32, 4096):   {"fused": "oneshot", "block_size": 4096},
    (16, 32768):  {"fused": "online",  "block_size": 4096},
    (8, 131072):  {"fused": False,     "nb": 16, "block_size": 1024},
    (4, 262144):  {"fused": False,     "nb": 32, "block_size": 1024},
}


@triton.jit
def softmax_oneshot_kernel(
    input_ptr,
    output_ptr,
    n_rows,
    n_cols,
    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
):
    """One-shot softmax for rows that fit in a single tile (n_cols <= BLOCK_SIZE).
    Loads the row once, computes max & sum, and writes the output.
    """
    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
    if row_idx >= n_rows:
        return

    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols

    cols = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
    mask = cols < n_cols
    x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
    row_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
    row_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - row_max), axis=0)
    out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
    tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)


@triton.jit
def softmax_fused_kernel(
    input_ptr,
    output_ptr,
    n_rows,
    n_cols,
    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
):
    """Two-pass online softmax for medium-length rows."""
    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
    if row_idx >= n_rows:
        return

    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols

    # Online softmax: single-pass max+sum.
    row_max = -float('inf')
    row_sum = 0.0
    offset = 0
    while offset < n_cols:
        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
        mask = cols < n_cols
        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
        row_max = new_max
        offset += BLOCK_SIZE

    # Second pass: write normalized output.
    offset = 0
    while offset < n_cols:
        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
        mask = cols < n_cols
        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
        offset += BLOCK_SIZE


@triton.jit
def softmax_max_kernel(
    input_ptr,
    mid_max_ptr,
    mid_sum_ptr,
    n_rows,
    n_cols,
    num_blocks_per_row,
    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
):
    pid = tl.program_id(0)
    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
    if row_idx >= n_rows:
        return

    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx

    local_max = -float('inf')
    local_sum = 0.0
    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
    while offset < n_cols:
        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
        mask = cols < n_cols
        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
        local_max = new_max
        offset += stride

    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)


@triton.jit
def softmax_reduce_kernel(
    mid_max_ptr,
    mid_sum_ptr,
    row_max_ptr,
    row_sum_ptr,
    n_rows,
    num_blocks_per_row,
):
    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
    if row_idx >= n_rows:
        return

    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
    global_max = -float('inf')
    global_sum = 0.0
    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
        global_max = new_max

    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)


@triton.jit
def softmax_write_kernel(
    input_ptr,
    output_ptr,
    row_max_ptr,
    row_sum_ptr,
    n_rows,
    n_cols,
    num_blocks_per_row,
    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
):
    pid = tl.program_id(0)
    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
    if row_idx >= n_rows:
        return

    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)

    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
    while offset < n_cols:
        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
        mask = cols < n_cols
        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
        offset += stride


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, batch: int, vocab: int):
        super().__init__()
        self.batch = batch
        self.vocab = vocab

        cfg = _KERNEL_CFG.get((batch, vocab))
        if cfg is None:
            if vocab <= 4096:
                cfg = {"fused": "oneshot", "block_size": 4096}
            elif vocab <= 32768:
                cfg = {"fused": "online", "block_size": 4096}
            else:
                nb = max(1, min(32, 128 // batch))
                cfg = {"fused": False, "nb": nb, "block_size": 1024}
        self._cfg = cfg

        # Pre-allocate scratch buffers for the multi-block path so that
        # repeated forward() calls avoid cudaMalloc overhead.
        if cfg.get("fused") is False:
            nb = cfg["nb"]
            self._mid_max = torch.empty(
                batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda"
            )
            self._mid_sum = torch.empty(
                batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda"
            )
            self._row_max = torch.empty(
                batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda"
            )
            self._row_sum = torch.empty(
                batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda"
            )

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        assert x.dim() == 2
        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
        out = torch.empty_like(x)
        cfg = self._cfg
        fused = cfg.get("fused")

        if fused == "oneshot":
            grid = (n_rows,)
            softmax_oneshot_kernel[grid](
                x, out,
                n_rows, n_cols,
                BLOCK_SIZE=cfg["block_size"],
            )
        elif fused == "online":
            grid = (n_rows,)
            softmax_fused_kernel[grid](
                x, out,
                n_rows, n_cols,
                BLOCK_SIZE=cfg["block_size"],
            )
        else:
            nb = cfg["nb"]
            bs = cfg["block_size"]
            mid_max = self._mid_max[: n_rows * nb]
            mid_sum = self._mid_sum[: n_rows * nb]
            row_max = self._row_max[:n_rows]
            row_sum = self._row_sum[:n_rows]

            grid1 = (n_rows * nb,)
            softmax_max_kernel[grid1](
                x, mid_max, mid_sum,
                n_rows, n_cols, nb,
                BLOCK_SIZE=bs,
            )
            grid2 = (n_rows,)
            softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](
                mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum,
                n_rows, nb,
            )
            grid3 = (n_rows * nb,)
            softmax_write_kernel[grid3](
                x, out, row_max, row_sum,
                n_rows, n_cols, nb,
                BLOCK_SIZE=bs,
            )
        return out


BATCH = 8
VOCAB = 32768


def get_inputs():
    x = torch.randn(BATCH, VOCAB, dtype=torch.float32) * 4.0
    return [x]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, VOCAB]

     1	I need you to write a numerically tight softmax for the RTX PRO 6000 (SM120 Blackwell, GDDR7, 1.8 TB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py.      3	The op is softmax along the last dim of a 2D fp32 tensor.      1	name: 04_kahan_softmax
     2	display_name: "Kahan-corrected Softmax"
     3	precision: fp32
     4	regime: memory  # softmax is bandwidth-bound: 2 passes over the input tensor

WriteFile /home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/solution.py
diff (92 lines)
--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/solution.py
@@ -0,0 +1,89 @@
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+OP_TYPE = "softmax"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    # --- Pass 1: compute row max ---
+    row_max = -float("inf")
+    for offset in range(0, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE):
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float("inf"))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        row_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+
+    # --- Pass 2: compute row sum with Kahan compensation ---
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    row_c = 0.0
+    for offset in range(0, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE):
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float("inf"))
+        exp_vals = tl.exp(x - row_max)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(exp_vals, axis=0)
+        # Kahan add block_sum into row_sum
+        y = block_sum - row_c
+        t = row_sum + y
+        row_c = (t - row_sum) - y
+        row_sum = t
+
+    # --- Pass 3: write output ---
+    for offset in range(0, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE):
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float("inf"))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch: int, vocab: int):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.vocab = vocab
+
+    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
+        assert x.dim() == 2
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        BLOCK_SIZE = 1024
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_kernel[grid](
+            x, out,
+            n_rows, n_cols,
+            BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE,
+        )
+        return out
+
+
+BATCH = 8
+VOCAB = 32768
+
+
+def get_inputs():
+    x = torch.randn(BATCH, VOCAB, dtype=torch.float32) * 4.0
+    return [x]
+
+
+def get_init_inputs():
+    return [BATCH, VOCAB]

Implementation details: ``` @triton.jit def softmax_max_kernel(input_ptr, row_max_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): pid = tl.program_id(0) row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols # initialize local max local_max = -float('inf') # grid-stride loop for offset in range(block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE): cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0) local_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max) # atomic max to global row max row_max = row_max_ptr + row_idx tl.atomic_max(row_max, local_max) ``` Then sum kernel: ``` @triton.jit def softmax_sum_kernel(input_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): pid = tl.program_id(0) row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx) local_sum = 0.0 local_c = 0.0 for offset in range(block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE): cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) exp_vals = tl.exp(x - row_max) block_sum = tl.sum(exp_vals, axis=0) # Kahan add y = block_sum - local_c t = local_sum + y local_c = (t - local_sum) - y local_sum = t tl.atomic_add(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, local_sum) ``` Then write kernel: ``` @triton.jit def softmax_write_kernel(input_ptr, output_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): pid = tl.program_id(0) row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx) row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx) for offset in range(block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE): cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask) ``` We need to allocate `row_max` and `row_sum` tensors. The `ptr` can be a scalar pointer or a tensor of pointers. For a scalar pointer, it should work. But we need to ensure that the block reduction `tl.max(x, axis=0)` returns a scalar (a 0-d tensor). In Triton, scalar operations are fine. One issue: `tl.atomic_max` for float might not be available on all backends. We saw it's in the API. Let's test it. Also, we need to be careful about the Triton compiler optimizing away loops or causing issues with `num_blocks_per_row` as a non-constexpr. In Triton, `range` loop bounds can be dynamic. The step must be a compile-time constant? Actually `range(start, stop, step)` requires `step` to be a constant in Triton 2.x. In Triton 3.x, dynamic step might be supported, but it's safer to make it a `tl.constexpr`. Since we want to vary it per launch, we need to compile multiple versions or keep it fixed. If we keep `num_blocks_per_row` fixed (e.g., 16 or 32), we can pass it as a `tl.constexpr`. The loop `range(block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE)` will have start >= stop, so it won't execute. That's fine. But if `num_blocks_per_row` is fixed to 32, for vocab=4096, each block processes 128 elements (BLOCK_SIZE=1024, but start is block_idx*1024, step is 32*1024=32768. Wait, for vocab=4096, block_idx*1024 can be >= 4096 for block_idx >= 4. So only blocks 0..3 do work. That's okay: the other blocks are idle. But we still launch 32 blocks per row. No, that doesn't work because the exp depends on the global max. Wait, there is a trick: we can compute local max and local sum of exp(x - local_max) for each block, storing both. Then in a second kernel, we combine the local maxes and sums using the log-sum-exp formula. Specifically: - For each block i: `m_i = max(x_i)`, `s_i = sum(exp(x_i - m_i))`. - Global max `M = max_i(m_i)`. - Global sum `S = sum_i(s_i * exp(m_i - M))`. This requires a second kernel that reads the per-block `m_i` and `s_i` and computes `M` and `S`. Then a third kernel writes output using `M` and `S`. But the second kernel is a reduction over `num_blocks_per_row` elements. That can be done with one block per row. For `num_blocks_per_row=32`, it's trivial. So: - Kernel 1: each block computes `m_i` and `s_i` (with local max and sum). Write to `mid_max` and `mid_sum`. - Kernel 2: one block per row reads `mid_max` and `mid_sum`, computes global `M` and `S`. Write to `row_max` and `row_sum`. - Kernel 3: each block reads `row_max` and `row_sum`, writes output. This avoids atomics entirely. Atomics can be slow or have precision issues? `atomic_max` for float might be implemented with compare-and-swap loops, which could be slower than a simple reduction. Also `atomic_add` for float can have rounding issues (the order of adds is non-deterministic). Since we need high accuracy, deterministic order is better. So the reduction buffer approach is preferable for accuracy. In Kernel 1, each block can compute local max and local sum in one pass? Wait, local sum needs local max. Since each block processes a relatively small chunk (e.g., 8192 elements), online softmax per block is accurate enough. But we can also just do two loops; the memory bandwidth is the same. Let's do online softmax per block in Kernel 1: ``` local_max = -inf local_sum = 0.0 for each chunk: x = load(...) # online update new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, tl.max(x)) # But we need to update sum for all elements in x. # For a chunk, we can compute chunk_max = tl.max(x) # scale = exp(local_max - chunk_max) # local_sum = local_sum * scale + sum(exp(x - chunk_max)) # local_max = chunk_max ``` But this requires a loop over chunks. For each chunk, we compute `chunk_max = tl.max(x)` and `chunk_sum = tl.sum(exp(x - chunk_max))`. Then we update the running max and sum: ``` scale = tl.exp(local_max - chunk_max) local_sum = local_sum * scale + chunk_sum local_max = chunk_max ``` This is exact (within fp32) per chunk. The error is small. Since each block processes at most, say, 8192 elements (8 chunks of 1024), the error is negligible. But note: `tl.exp(local_max - chunk_max)` could be very small if `chunk_max` is much larger than `local_max`. That's fine. If `local_max` is larger, `scale` is >1? If it's smaller than the running max, we scale the current sum up and add the new chunk's sum (which is computed relative to its own max). This is the standard online softmax update. It works. Kernel 3: - Each block reads `row_max` and `row_sum`. - Loop over chunks, compute `exp(x - row_max) / row_sum`, write output. This is clean, no atomics, deterministic, and should be fast. We need to decide `num_blocks_per_row` and `BLOCK_SIZE`. We want each block to do enough work to amortize overhead, but not too little. Let's set `BLOCK_SIZE = 1024`. Then `num_blocks_per_row` can be chosen so that total elements per block is around 4096-8192. For vocab=262144, `num_blocks_per_row = 32` => 8192 elements per block. But `num_blocks_per_row` appears as a `tl.constexpr` in the kernel if we use it in stride calculations in a `for` loop. However, we can use a `while` loop and pass it as a normal argument. Let's design the kernel with `while` loops so we can pass `num_blocks_per_row` as a normal integer. ``` @triton.jit def softmax_max_kernel(input_ptr, mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): pid = tl.program_id(0) row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx # compute block max local_max = -float('inf') offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE while offset < n_cols: cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0) local_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max) offset += stride # compute block sum local_sum = 0.0 local_c = 0.0 offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE while offset < n_cols: cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) exp_vals = tl.exp(x - local_max) block_sum = tl.sum(exp_vals, axis=0) y = block_sum - local_c t = local_sum + y local_c = (t - local_sum) - y local_sum = t offset += stride tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max) tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum) ``` Kernel 2: ``` @triton.jit def softmax_reduce_kernel(mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr, n_rows, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): row_idx = tl.program_id(0) if row_idx >= n_rows: return base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row # load all mid values for this row # We can load up to BLOCK_SIZE values. num_blocks_per_row is at most 32. # Let's use a loop. global_max = -float('inf') # first find global max for i in range(0, num_blocks_per_row, 1): mid_max = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i) global_max = tl.maximum(global_max, mid_max) # now compute global sum global_sum = 0.0 global_c = 0.0 for i in range(0, num_blocks_per_row, 1): mid_max = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i) mid_sum = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i) val = mid_sum * tl.exp(mid_max - global_max) y = val - global_c t = global_sum + y global_c = (t - global_sum) - y global_sum = t tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max) tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum) ``` Wait, `for i in range(0, num_blocks_per_row, 1)` requires `num_blocks_per_row` to be a `tl.constexpr` in older Triton versions? In Triton 3.x, dynamic loop bounds are supported in `for` loops. But the step must be constexpr. Step=1 is a constant. The bound `num_blocks_per_row` can be dynamic. I think this works. But to be safe, we can use a `while` loop. Also, in Kernel 2, each block only processes one row. So we launch `n_rows` blocks. That's fine. Kernel 3: ``` @triton.jit def softmax_write_kernel(input_ptr, output_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): pid = tl.program_id(0) row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx) row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx) offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE while offset < n_cols: cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask) offset += stride ``` This looks good. We need to allocate `mid_max`, `mid_sum`, `row_max`, `row_sum`. `mid_max` shape = (batch, num_blocks_per_row). We can allocate them in the forward method. One concern: in Kernel 1, we read the input twice per block. With many blocks, total reads = 2 * batch * vocab. Then Kernel 3 reads again. Total reads = 3 * batch * vocab. The benchmark's bytes formula assumes 1 read + 1 write. So our reported gbps will be lower. But actual time might still be good if bandwidth is saturated. Can we fuse the block sum computation with the block max computation in a single read using online softmax per block? Yes. Let's do that. It reduces reads in Kernel 1 from 2 to 1. Then total reads = 2 * batch * vocab (1 in Kernel 1, 1 in Kernel 3). That's better. Online softmax per block: ``` local_max = -float('inf') local_sum = 0.0 offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE while offset < n_cols: cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0) block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0) # update running max and sum new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max) scale = tl.exp(local_max - new_max) local_sum = local_sum * scale + block_sum * tl.exp(block_max - new_max) local_max = new_max offset += stride ``` Wait, the standard online softmax update is: ``` m_new = max(m, x_i) d = d * exp(m - m_new) + exp(x_i - m_new) ``` For a block of elements, we have block_max and block_sum = sum(exp(x - block_max)). If `local_max <= block_max`: `new_max = block_max` `scale = exp(local_max - block_max)` `local_sum = local_sum * scale + block_sum` If `local_max > block_max`: `new_max = local_max` `scale = exp(block_max - local_max)` `local_sum = local_sum + block_sum * scale` We can write it uniformly: ``` new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max) scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max) scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max) local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block local_max = new_max ``` This is correct. Let's verify: - If local_max = -inf, scale_local = 0, scale_block = exp(block_max - block_max) = 1. Then local_sum = 0 + block_sum * 1 = block_sum. local_max = block_max. Good. - If local_max > block_max, scale_local = exp(local_max - local_max) = 1, scale_block = exp(block_max - local_max). Then local_sum = local_sum + block_sum * scale_block. Good. - If local_max < block_max, scale_local = exp(local_max - block_max), scale_block = 1. Then local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum. Good. This is exact in fp32 (subject to rounding in exp and multiply-add). Since each block processes at most ~8 chunks, the rounding error is tiny. So Kernel 1 can be: ``` local_max = -float('inf') local_sum = 0.0 offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE while offset < n_cols: cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0) block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0) new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max) scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max) scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max) local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block local_max = new_max offset += stride ``` Then write `local_max` and `local_sum` to mid buffers. This reads the input once per block. Great. Now Kernel 2 reduces the per-block max and sum to global max and sum. We can also use the same online formula: ``` global_max = -float('inf') global_sum = 0.0 for i in range(num_blocks_per_row): m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i) s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i) new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m) scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max) scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max) global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m global_max = new_max ``` This is a loop over `num_blocks_per_row` (up to 32). Since it's done by a single block per row, the loop is sequential within the block. That's fine. Kernel 3 writes output with one read. Total reads = 2 * batch * vocab. Writes = 1 * batch * vocab. Plus the intermediate writes/reads of mid buffers (batch * num_blocks_per_row * 4 bytes each). For num_blocks_per_row=32 and batch=4, that's 512 bytes, negligible. So memory traffic is dominated by 2 reads + 1 write. That's 50% more than the benchmark formula, but it's the best we can do with a two-level reduction. Wait, can we do a single-pass online softmax across the entire row with multi-block? That's the atomic approach. But with the reduction buffer approach, we need the intermediate reduction. import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_kernel(ptr, n, BLOCK: tl.constexpr):
    pid = tl.program_id(0)
    off = pid * BLOCK
    i = 0
    while i < 3:
        off = off + 1
        i = i + 1
    tl.store(ptr, off)

import torch

print('ok')

+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def test_kernel(ptr, n, BLOCK: tl.constexpr):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    off = pid * BLOCK
+    i = 0
+    while i < 3:
+        off = off + 1
+        i = i + 1

reasoning (610 chars)
Good, while loops work. Now let's implement the multi-block kernel. We need to be careful about the `num_blocks_per_row` parameter. Since we want to vary it per shape, we can pass it as a normal integer. The kernels will use while loops. But compiling kernels with dynamic values for `num_blocks_per_row` might cause recompilation each time if the value changes. That's fine; there are only a few shapes. However, the `range` loop in Kernel 2 (reduce) uses `num_blocks_per_row` as the bound. In Triton, `for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):` where `num_blocks_per_row` is not constexpr might work. Let's test.

+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+def softmax_multi(x, num_blocks_per_row=32, BLOCK_SIZE=1024):
+    n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+    out = torch.empty_like(x)
+    mid_max = torch.empty(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+    mid_sum = torch.empty(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+    row_max = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+    row_sum = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+
+    grid1 = (n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)
+    softmax_max_kernel[grid1](
+        x, mid_max, mid_sum,
+        n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row,
+        BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE,
+    )
+    grid2 = (n_rows,)
+    softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](
+        mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum,
+        n_rows, num_blocks_per_row,
+    )
+    grid3 = (n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)
+    softmax_write_kernel[grid3](
+        x, out, row_max, row_sum,
+        n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row,
+        BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE,
+    )
+    return out
+
+
+def reference(x):
+    x64 = x.to(torch.float64)
+    m = x64.amax(dim=-1, keepdim=True)
+    e = torch.exp(x64 - m)
+    s = e.sum(dim=-1, keepdim=True)
+    return (e / s).to(torch.float32)
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    for batch, vocab in [(32, 4096), (16, 32768), (8, 131072), (4, 262144)]:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab, dtype=torch.float32, device='cuda') * 4.0
+        y = softmax_multi(x, num_blocks_per_row=32)
+        y_ref = reference(x)
+        diff = (y - y_ref).abs().max().item()
+        print(f"batch={batch} vocab={vocab} max_diff={diff:.2e}")
+        assert diff < 1e-5
+    print("all passed")
args

assistant
reasoning (3005 chars)
The geomean is 0.0806, still below 0.1. The small shapes (0 and 1) are dragging it down. For shape 0 (batch=32, vocab=4096), num_blocks_per_row=1, so we are using the single-block kernel. Performance is 0.019 peak_fraction. For shape 1 (batch=16, vocab=32768), num_blocks_per_row=8? Wait, heuristic: (32768+4095)//4096 = 8. So num_blocks_per_row=8. Performance is 0.0523. For shapes 2,3,4 (larger), performance is great: ~0.138-0.157. So the bottleneck is the smaller shapes. Let's analyze why small shapes are slow. For shape 0: batch=32, vocab=4096. num_blocks_per_row=1. The kernel does: - Kernel 1: 32 blocks. Each block loops 4 times (4096/1024). Computes online max/sum. - Kernel 2: 32 blocks. Each block loops over num_blocks_per_row=1. Trivial. - Kernel 3: 32 blocks. Each block loops 4 times. Writes output. Total blocks = 32. That's few. The time is 0.031 ms. The naive single-block kernel earlier took 0.021 ms. So the multi-block approach is actually slower for shape 0 due to 3 kernels. But 0.021 ms was also low (0.027 peak_fraction). The issue is that for small tensors, overhead dominates. The benchmark's bytes formula is `batch * vocab * 8`. For shape 0: 32*4096*8 = 1,048,576 bytes = 1 MB. At 1.8 TB/s, theoretical time = 0.58 microseconds. Our kernel takes ~30 microseconds, which is ~50x slower. This is due to kernel launch overhead and underutilization. But the reference eager also takes 68 microseconds, compiled takes 105, sota takes 76. So our 31 is actually faster than reference. But the peak_fraction is low because the benchmark expects near-peak bandwidth even for tiny sizes? Actually the peak_fraction is computed using the formula bytes / time. For 1 MB, to get peak_fraction >= 0.1, we need gbps >= 180 GB/s. Time <= 1 MB / 180 GB/s = 5.8 microseconds. That's very aggressive for a 1MB tensor; kernel launch overhead alone is ~5-10 microseconds. So getting >0.1 on tiny shapes is nearly impossible with discrete kernels. But maybe we can fuse the three kernels into one? Or use torch.compile? But we need a custom kernel. Alternatively, we can use a single kernel that does everything with persistent threads and cross-block sync via atomics. That would reduce launch overhead. But cross-block sync within a single kernel is tricky. However, for small batch sizes, 3 kernel launches is not too bad. For shape 0, 3 launches might be okay if each is fast. If num_blocks_per_row=1, then each row is processed by a single block. In that case, the block can compute max, sum, and write output all in one kernel, just like the naive solution. That would reduce launches from 3 to 1 for small shapes. For larger shapes with num_blocks_per_row > 1, we need the multi-kernel approach. So we can branch in the forward method: if `num_blocks_per_row == 1`, use the fused single-block kernel. If > 1, use the 3-kernel approach. Let's write a fused single-block kernel: ``` @triton.jit def softmax_fused_kernel(input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): row_idx = tl.program_id(0) if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols # online softmax row_max = -float('inf') row_sum = 0.0 for offset in range(0, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE): cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0) block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0) new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max) scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max) scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max) row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block row_max = new_max # write output for offset in range(0, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE): cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask) ``` This is exactly the naive solution but using online softmax (single read). Wait, the naive solution had 3 reads (max, sum, write). This fused version has 2 reads (online sum, write). So it should be faster. For shape 0, this should give better performance. Let's test it. For shape 1, num_blocks_per_row = 8. We still need 3 kernels. But maybe we can increase num_blocks_per_row for shape 1 to improve parallelism? +import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+import time
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+def fused(x):
+    n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+    out = torch.empty_like(x)
+    grid = (n_rows,)
+    softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=1024)
+    return out
+
+
+def multi(x, num_blocks_per_row=32):
+    n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+    out = torch.empty_like(x)
+    mid_max = torch.empty(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+    mid_sum = torch.empty(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+    row_max = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+    row_sum = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+
+    grid1 = (n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)
+    softmax_max_kernel[grid1](x, mid_max, mid_sum, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE=1024)
+    grid2 = (n_rows,)
+    softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, num_blocks_per_row)
+    grid3 = (n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)
+    softmax_write_kernel[grid3](x, out, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE=1024)
+    return out
+
+
+def time_it(fn, x, iters=100):
+    # warmup
+    for _ in range(10):
+        fn(x)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    start = time.perf_counter()
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        fn(x)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    end = time.perf_counter()
+    return (end - start) / iters * 1000
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    for batch, vocab in [(32, 4096), (16, 32768), (8, 131072), (4, 262144)]:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab, dtype=torch.float32, device='cuda') * 4.0
+        t_fused = time_it(fused, x)
+        t_multi_8 = time_it(lambda x

reasoning (4370 chars)
Great! With the best config per shape, geomean would be ~0.154, well above 0.1. So we just need to integrate the tuning into solution.py. The simplest robust approach: use a hybrid. For `n_cols <= 8192`, use the fused single-block kernel. For `n_cols > 8192`, use the multi-block approach with `num_blocks_per_row` chosen as a power of 2 that gives good performance. From the tuning: - vocab=32768: nb=2 or 16 both ~0.022ms. nb=2 gives total blocks=32. nb=16 gives total blocks=256. Let's pick nb=8? Actually nb=8 gave 0.0253ms, slightly slower. nb=2 is fine. - vocab=131072: nb=8 or 32 both ~0.022ms. nb=8 gives total blocks=64. nb=32 gives total blocks=256. Let's pick nb=8. - vocab=262144: nb=16 is best at 0.0219ms. nb=8 is 0.0264ms. So nb=16. Heuristic: `num_blocks_per_row = max(1, min(32, n_cols // 16384))` gives: - 32768 -> 2 - 131072 -> 8 - 262144 -> 16 Perfect! That matches the best configs. Let's test this heuristic. For n_cols=32768, 32768//16384 = 2. Good. For n_cols=131072, 131072//16384 = 8. Good. For n_cols=262144, 262144//16384 = 16. Good. For n_cols=4096, 4096//16384 = 0 -> max(1, ...) = 1. But we will use fused kernel for <=8192. What about n_cols=8192? 8192//16384 = 0 -> 1. Fused kernel will be used for <=8192. What about n_cols=65536? 65536//16384 = 4. That seems reasonable. What about n_cols=1048576? 1048576//16384 = 64 -> min(32, 64) = 32. Fine. So the heuristic is: ``` if n_cols <= 8192: use fused kernel with 1 block per row else: num_blocks_per_row = max(1, min(32, n_cols // 16384)) use multi-block kernel ``` But wait, for shape 1 (32768), nb=2 gave 0.0222ms, which is slightly faster than fused (0.0238ms). Using nb=2 is fine. But we need to make sure that with nb=2, the multi-block kernel overhead is not too high. The test showed it's okay. Alternatively, we could always use the multi-block kernel for n_cols > 4096. But for n_cols=4096, nb=1 means multi-block is same as fused but with 3 kernels. The test showed nb=1 multi is 0.022ms vs fused 0.0068ms. So fused is much better for small sizes. So we should definitely use fused for small sizes. Let's set threshold at 8192. For n_cols <= 8192, fused. For n_cols > 8192, multi with nb = max(1, min(32, n_cols // 16384)). But for n_cols just above 8192, e.g., 12288, nb = 12288 // 16384 = 0 -> 1. So multi with nb=1. That means 3 kernels for a medium size. The fused kernel would be faster. But our benchmark doesn't have such a shape. So it's okay. We could also compute nb = max(1, min(32, (n_cols + 8191) // 16384)). For 12288, that's 1. For 32768, 2. For 131072, 8. For 262144, 16. Same. Let's implement this in solution.py. One concern: the fused kernel uses a `while` loop with `offset < n_cols`. For n_cols=4096, it loops 4 times. That's fine. For n_cols=8192, it loops 8 times. Also fine. Wait, in the fused kernel, the online softmax update might have issues if `n_cols` is not a multiple of BLOCK_SIZE and the last block contains `-inf` from the mask. `tl.max(x, axis=0)` with `other=-float('inf')` returns the correct max. `tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)` with `other=-float('inf')` gives `exp(-inf) = 0` for masked elements, so sum is correct. But in the fused kernel, we need to be careful about `tl.exp(row_max - new_max)` when `row_max = -inf` initially. `tl.exp(-inf - new_max) = 0`. So `row_sum = row_sum * 0 + block_sum * scale_block`. If `new_max = block_max`, `scale_block = exp(block_max - block_max) = 1`. So `row_sum = block_sum`. Good. One more thing: in the multi-block kernel, we have `mid_max` and `mid_sum` buffers. We need to initialize them? Actually we write to all entries in Kernel 1. So no need to initialize. In Kernel 2, we loop over `num_blocks_per_row` elements. Since we wrote all of them in Kernel 1, it's safe. Potential issue: Triton kernel compilation time. Since we have two different kernels (fused and multi), and the multi kernel is compiled with different `num_blocks_per_row` values (which are dynamic, not constexpr), the compilation might happen once per unique `num_blocks_per_row` value. That's okay. But for the fused kernel, the grid is `(n_rows,)`. For the multi-block kernel, the grid is `(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)`. All fine. Let's also test correctness of the hybrid approach on extreme logits. We should test shape 4 (extreme). Let's modify the test to include extreme.

+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+def forward(x):
+    n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+    out = torch.empty_like(x)
+    if n_cols <= 8192:
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=1024)
+    else:
+        num_blocks_per_row = max(1, min(32, n_cols // 16384))
+        mid_max = torch.empty(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        mid_sum = torch.empty(n_rows * num_blocks_per_row, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        row_max = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        row_sum = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+
+        grid1 = (n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)
+        softmax_max_kernel[grid1](
+            x, mid_max, mid_sum,
+            n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row,
+            BLOCK_SIZE=1024,
+        )
+        grid2 = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](
+            mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum,
+            n_rows, num_blocks_per_row,
+        )
+        grid3 = (n_rows * num_blocks_per_row,)
+        softmax_write_kernel[grid3](
+            x, out, row_max, row_sum,
+            n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row,
+            BLOCK_SIZE=1024,
+        )
+    return out
+
+
+def reference(x):
+    x64 = x.to(torch.float64)
+    m = x64.amax(dim=-1, keepdim=True)
+    e = torch.exp(x64 - m)
+    s = e.sum(dim=-1, keepdim=True)
+    return (e / s).to(torch.float32)
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    shapes = [
+        (32, 4096, False),
+        (16, 32768, False),
+        (8, 131072, False),
+        (4, 262144, False),
+        (8, 131072, True),
+    ]
+    for b

 OP_TYPE = "softmax"
 SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
 HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    # Online softmax: single-pass max+sum.
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+    # Second pass: write normalized output.
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE

The hardware block size is determined by the compiler. You can set BLOCK_SIZE to values larger than 1024, and Triton will handle it by using loops within the block. For example, BLOCK_SIZE=2048 might be compiled as two iterations of 1024 per block. This could reduce loop overhead in the source code but not necessarily improve performance. But Triton doesn't have a 2D grid for rows; we can use a 1D grid where each block handles a range of rows. ``` row_start_idx = tl.program_id(0) * ROWS_PER_BLOCK for r in range(ROWS_PER_BLOCK): row_idx = row_start_idx + r if row_idx >= n_rows: break ... process row ... ``` This is a loop over rows within a block. But for large shapes (batch=4), we might have only 1 block doing 4 rows, which would be bad for parallelism. So we should only use this multi-row-per-block for small total sizes. With 1 block per row, threads within a block access consecutive elements. That's coalesced. With multiple rows per block, threads still access consecutive elements within a row, but there might be divergence between rows if they are processed sequentially within the block. However, since all threads in the block process the same row at the same time (if we loop over rows, the whole block works on one row), it's fine. So all threads process row 0 together, then row 1 together, etc. That's fine. But the `row_idx` would vary across blocks. The memory accesses for each row are independent but contiguous within the row. Let's test a fused kernel with `rows_per_block`.
WriteFile /home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_rows_per_block.py
diff (89 lines)
--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_rows_per_block.py
@@ -0,0 +1,86 @@
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+import time
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_rows_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    ROWS_PER_BLOCK: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    block_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_start_idx = block_idx * ROWS_PER_BLOCK
+    if row_start_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    for r in range(ROWS_PER_BLOCK):
+        row_idx = row_start_idx + r
+        if row_idx >= n_rows:
+            break
+        row_in = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+        row_out = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+        row_max = -float('inf')
+        row_sum = 0.0
+        offset = 0
+        while offset < n_cols:
+            cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+            mask = cols < n_cols
+            x = tl.load(row_in + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+            block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+            block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+            new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+            scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+            scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+            row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+            row_max = new_max
+            offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+        offset = 0
+        while offset < n_cols:
+            cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+            mask = cols < n_cols
+            x = tl.load(row_in + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+            out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+            tl.store(row_out + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+            offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+def fused_rows(x, rows_per_block=1):
+    n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+    out = torch.empty_like(x)
+    grid = ((n_rows + rows_per_block - 1) // rows_per_block,)
+    softmax_fused_rows_kernel[grid](
+        x, out, n_rows, n_cols,
+        ROWS_PER_BLOCK=rows_per_block,
+        BLOCK_SIZE=1024,
+    )
+    return out
+
+
+def time_it(fn, x, iters=200):
+    for _ in range(20):
+        fn(x)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    start = time.perf_counter()
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        fn(x)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    end = time.perf_counter()
+    return (end - start) / iters * 1000
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    for batch, vocab in [(32, 4096), (16, 32768)]:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab, dtype=torch.float32, device='cuda') * 4.0
+        print(f"\nbatch={batch} vocab={vocab}")
+        for rpb in [1, 2, 4, 8, 16, 32]:
+            if rpb > batch:
+                continue
+            t = time_it(lambda x: fused_rows(x, rpb), x)
+            print(f"  rows_per_block={rpb:2d} -> {t:.4f}ms")

reasoning (2121 chars)
Triton doesn't support `break` in loops. We can avoid `break` by ensuring the grid size is exact (no out-of-bounds rows). Since we compute grid = `(n_rows + rows_per_block - 1) // rows_per_block`, the last block might have fewer rows. We can handle it by adding a conditional `if row_idx < n_rows:` inside the loop, but without `break`. However, if `ROWS_PER_BLOCK` is a constexpr, the loop will iterate `ROWS_PER_BLOCK` times. For the last block, some rows are out of bounds. We can just skip them with `if row_idx < n_rows:` but we can't break. That's fine; the out-of-bounds iterations will just do nothing (or we need to guard all loads/stores). But we can also compute grid = `n_rows // rows_per_block` and handle the remainder with a separate kernel launch. That's overkill. Simpler: we can just not use rows_per_block and instead tune BLOCK_SIZE or use vectorized loads. Actually, the fused kernel for shape 0 is already quite fast: 0.012 ms in benchmark, which is 85.9 gbps. The problem is that 85.9 gbps is only 4.8% of 1800 gbps. For a 1MB tensor, that's expected. The benchmark's OK threshold is 0.1 geomean. If we can't get shape 0 above, say, 0.06, we need the other shapes to be much higher. Let's see what geomean we need: If shape0=0.05, shape1=0.05, shape2=0.20, shape3=0.20, shape4=0.20: geomean = (0.05*0.05*0.2*0.2*0.2)^(1/5) = (0.00002)^(0.2) = exp(0.2 * ln(2e-5)) = exp(0.2 * (-10.82)) = exp(-2.164) = 0.115. So if we can get shape2-4 to ~0.20 and shape0-1 to ~0.05, we pass. Currently shape2=0.1548, shape3=0.1260, shape4=0.1203. These are lower than the 0.20 we saw in the tuning test. Why? reasoning (7490 chars)
Ah, the benchmark does L2 flush between each timed call! That means it measures pure HBM bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth. For small tensors that fit in L2, the L2 flush makes the effective bandwidth lower because the data must be fetched from HBM every time. This explains why small shapes have low peak_fraction. For large shapes, L2 flush still matters but the kernel is more compute/bandwidth bound. Our tuning test didn't do L2 flush, so it was faster due to L2 caching. The benchmark's numbers are the ground truth. So we need to optimize for the L2-flushed scenario. The key is to minimize total memory traffic, because every byte must come from HBM. Our fused kernel reads the input twice (online pass + write pass) and writes output once. Total traffic = 3 * batch * vocab * 4 bytes = 12 * batch * vocab bytes. But the benchmark formula assumes 8 * batch * vocab bytes (read + write). So our effective gbps as reported by the benchmark is (8 / 12) * actual_bandwidth_utilization = 0.667 * actual_bw. If we could reduce reads to 1 (online) + 1 (write) = 2 reads, that's 3 * 4 = 12 bytes per element? Wait, read once (4 bytes), write once (4 bytes) = 8 bytes. But online softmax reads once, then write once. So total traffic = 8 bytes per element. That's what the benchmark formula assumes. So if we use a single-pass online softmax and write output, the total memory traffic is exactly 8 bytes per element. Our fused kernel already does that! Wait, the fused kernel does online pass (reads input) and write pass (reads input again + writes output). That's 2 reads + 1 write = 12 bytes per element. But online softmax can be done in a single pass: read x, compute running max and sum, but you can't write output until you know the final sum. So you need a second pass to write output. That's 2 reads + 1 write. However, there is a way to do it in one pass if you first compute max and sum, store them, and then write output in the same kernel but after the max/sum loop. That's still 2 reads + 1 write. The first read is for max/sum, the second read is for writing output. So 12 bytes per element. But wait, in the fused kernel, we are using `while` loops. For `n_cols <= 8192`, the online pass loops over the row. Then the write pass loops again. That's 2 reads. Can we do a single read by keeping the input in registers/shared memory between the two passes? For BLOCK_SIZE=1024, we would need to store 1024 floats per block. In Triton, we can load a block into a local tensor and reuse it. But the max/sum loop processes the entire row in chunks. If we load a chunk, compute its contribution to max/sum, and then store the chunk in a shared memory buffer, we could write output later. But we need the final global max and sum before writing. So we could do: 1. Loop over all chunks to compute global max and sum. 2. Loop over all chunks again, load from input (second read), compute output, write. We can't avoid the second read unless we cache the entire row. For vocab=4096, a row is 16 KB. We could cache it in shared memory. For vocab=32768, a row is 128 KB. That's too large for shared memory (max ~228 KB per SM, but per block it's limited). We could use global memory as a scratchpad, but that's extra writes/reads. For small shapes (vocab=4096), we could cache the entire row in shared memory to avoid the second read. But is it worth it? 16 KB is small. If we load it once into shared memory, compute max/sum, then read from shared memory to write output, total HBM traffic = read 16 KB + write 16 KB = 32 KB. Without caching, it's read 32 KB + write 16 KB = 48 KB. That's a 33% reduction. For 32768, row is 128 KB. Shared memory per block might be limited, but we can use multiple blocks per row and have each block cache its chunk. But that doesn't reduce total HBM reads. Wait, each block in the multi-block path already reads each chunk only once (online pass) and then reads again in the write pass. So 2 reads. Total HBM = 12 bytes/element. For large shapes, this is the bottleneck. If we want to match the benchmark formula (8 bytes/element), we need to read only once. The only way is to compute max and sum in a separate kernel (1 read), then write output using that max and sum (1 read + 1 write). That's still 2 reads + 1 write = 12 bytes/element. Wait, the first kernel reads once but doesn't write the input back. The second kernel reads once and writes once. So total = 2 reads + 1 write. That's 12 bytes. Actually, the benchmark formula `batch * vocab * 4 + batch * vocab * 4` is 8 bytes/element. This assumes you can compute softmax with one read and one write. Is that possible? Only if you can compute the output in a single pass without reading again. But you need the row sum to normalize. For online softmax, you can compute running max and sum, and when you finish the row, you know the final max and sum. But you can't write the output until then. Unless you write the output in a second pass (read again) or you keep the entire row in on-chip memory. So the benchmark formula is optimistic. However, Liger kernel's softmax (SOTA) might also do 2 reads + 1 write. But the benchmark formula is fixed. So to get a high peak_fraction, we need to minimize the actual time, not the bytes moved. The bytes moved in the formula is just a constant; the variable is time. So the key is to make the kernel as fast as possible. For small shapes, L2 flush dominates because the data is small and the kernel launch overhead + L2 flush time is comparable to the kernel execution time. The `time_fn` does: - L2 flush: writes 128 MB. That's a significant amount of time. For a kernel that processes 1 MB, the L2 flush takes much longer. - Then runs the kernel. So the total time is dominated by the L2 flush. The L2 flush is done for every trial. It writes 128 MB at ~1800 GB/s, taking ~71 microseconds. Our kernel for shape 0 takes ~12 microseconds. So total time per trial is ~83 microseconds. The benchmark reports median of 30 trials. So the reported time is ~0.083 ms. Wait, benchmark reported 0.012 ms for shape 0 solution. Let's re-examine. Wait, benchmark.py calls `time_fn(sol_model, inputs, iters=num_perf_trials)`. `time_fn` measures the time of `fn(*inputs)` only, using cuda events. The L2 flush is done before the event record, so it's not included in the measured time. The L2 flush evicts cache so that the kernel's memory accesses go to HBM. So the measured time is just the kernel execution time with cold L2. The L2 flush time is not included. For shape 0, the data is 1 MB. The L2 is 96 MB. After flushing L2, the next kernel run will read the 1 MB from HBM. But because the L2 is empty, the read goes to HBM. However, the write (output) might be cached. But the benchmark wants HBM bandwidth measurement. So for shape 0, with cold L2, reading 1 MB from HBM at 1800 GB/s takes 0.56 microseconds. Writing 0.5 MB takes 0.28 us. Total memory time ~0.84 us. Our kernel takes 12 us. That's ~14x slower than theoretical memory time. The overhead is due to kernel launch latency and loop overhead. For large shapes, memory time dominates. --- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_timing.py
@@ -0,0 +1,45 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+from solution import Model
+
+
+def _make_inputs(batch: int, vocab: int, extreme: bool):
+    if extreme:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 2.0
+        idx = torch.randint(0, vocab, (batch, 4))
+        x.scatter_(1, idx, 30.0)
+    else:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 4.0
+    return x.to(torch.float32)
+
+
+def main():
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    shapes = [
+        (32, 4096, False),
+        (16, 32768, False),
+        (8, 131072, False),
+        (4, 262144, False),
+        (8, 131072, True),
+    ]
+    for batch, vocab, extreme in shapes:
+        torch.manual_seed(2026)
+        x = _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme).to(device)
+        model = Model(batch, vocab).to(device).eval()
+        # warmup
+        with torch.no_grad():
+            _ = model(x)
+        t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+        bytes_moved = batch * vocab * 8
+        gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+        peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+        print(f"batch={batch:3d} vocab={vocab:6d} extreme={extreme} ms={t:.4f} gbps={gbps:.1f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

WriteFile /home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_fused_timing.py
diff (99 lines)
--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_fused_timing.py
@@ -0,0 +1,96 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+class FusedModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch, vocab):
+        super().__init__()
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=1024)
+        return out
+
+
+def _make_inputs(batch: int, vocab: int, extreme: bool):
+    if extreme:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 2.0
+        idx = torch.randint(0, vocab, (batch, 4))
+        x.scatter_(1, idx, 30.0)
+    else:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 4.0
+    return x.to(torch.float32)
+
+
+def main():
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    shapes = [
+        (32, 4096, False),
+        (16, 32768, False),
+        (8, 131072, False),
+        (4, 262144, False),
+        (8, 131072, True),
+    ]
+    for batch, vocab, extreme in shapes:
+        torch.manual_seed(2026)
+        x = _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme).to(device)
+        model = FusedModel(batch, vocab).to(device).eval()
+        with torch.no_grad():
+            _ = model(x)
+        t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+        bytes_moved = batch * vocab * 8
+        gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+        peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+        print(f"batch={batch:3d} vocab={vocab:6d} extreme={extreme} ms={t:.4f} gbps={gbps:.1f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_nb_heuristic.py
@@ -0,0 +1,182 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+# copy kernels from solution.py for standalone testing
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+class TestModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch, vocab, nb):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.vocab = vocab
+        self.nb = nb
+        if vocab > 8192:
+            self._mid_max = torch.empty(batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._mid_sum = torch.empty(batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._row_max = torch.empty(batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._row_sum = torch.empty(batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        BLOCK_SIZE = 1024
+        if n_cols <= 8192:
+            # fused single-block (not used here)
+            pass
+        else:
+            nb = self.nb
+            mid_max = self._mid_max[: n_rows * nb]
+            mid_sum = self._mid_sum[: n_rows * nb]
+            row_max = self._row_max[:n_rows]
+            row_sum = self._row_sum[:n_rows]
+            grid1 = (n_rows * nb,)
+            softmax_max_kernel[grid1](x, mid_max, mid_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE)
+            grid2 = (n_rows,)
+            softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, nb)
+            grid3 = (n_rows * nb,)
+            softmax_write_kernel[grid3](x, out, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE)
+        return out
+
+
+def _make_inputs(batch: int, vocab: int, extreme: bool):
+    if extreme:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 2.0
+        idx = torch.randint(0, vocab, (batch, 4))
+        x.scatter_(1, idx, 30.0)
+    else:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 4.0
+    return x.to(torch.float32)
+
+
+def main():
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    shapes = [
+        (16, 32768, False),
+        (8, 131072, False),
+        (4, 262144, False),
+    ]
+    for batch, vocab, extreme in shapes:
+        torch.manual_seed(2026)
+        x = _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme).to(device)
+        print(f"\nbatch={batch} vocab={vocab}")
+        for nb in [1, 2, 4, 8, 16, 32]:
+            model = TestModel(batch, vocab, nb).to(device).eval()
+            with torch.no_grad():
+                _ = model(x)
+            t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+            bytes_moved = batch * vocab * 8
+            gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+            peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+            print(f"  nb={nb:2d} ms={t:.4f} gbps={gbps:.1f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

So nb=16 is best. - (4, 262144): nb=32 gives 0.1729. nb=16 gives 0.1362. So nb=32 is best. This suggests that we want more blocks for larger vocab, but also for smaller batch. A heuristic that matches: - For (16, 32768): target total blocks ~128 (16*8). - For (8, 131072): target total blocks ~128 (8*16). - For (4, 262144): target total blocks ~128 (4*32). So total blocks ~128 is the sweet spot. We can set `num_blocks_per_row = max(1, min(32, 128 // batch))`. Let's test this heuristic: - batch=32: nb = max(1, min(32, 4)) = 4. But for vocab=4096, we use fused. So not applicable. - batch=16: nb = max(1, min(32, 8)) = 8. Matches best. - batch=8: nb = max(1, min(32, 16)) = 16. Matches best. - batch=4: nb = max(1, min(32, 32)) = 32. Matches best. But we also need to cap nb so that each block does enough work. For vocab=32768 and nb=8, each block processes 4096 elements.
