What about a hypothetical shape with batch=1, vocab=262144? nb=32, each block 8192. Fine. What about batch=32, vocab=131072? nb=4, each block 32768. That might be okay. So the heuristic `num_blocks_per_row = max(1, min(32, 128 // n_rows))` seems good. But we also need to handle shape0 (32, 4096) where fused is best. The fused kernel currently gives 0.043 peak_frac. Could we improve shape0 by using multi-block with nb=4? Since vocab=4096 <= 8192, our fused kernel uses 1 block per row. But maybe multi-block with nb=4 could be better? +import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+# Fused kernel with configurable BLOCK_SIZE
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+# Multi-block kernels with configurable BLOCK_SIZE
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr,
+    mid_sum_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    row_max_ptr,
+    row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    num_blocks_per_row,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+class TestModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch, vocab, nb, block_size):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.vocab = vocab
+        self.nb = nb
+        self.block_size = block_size
+        if vocab > 8192:
+            self._mid_max = torch.empty(batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._mid_sum = torch.empty(batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._row_max = torch.empty(batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._row_sum = torch.empty(batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        BLOCK_SIZE = self.block_size
+        if n_cols <= 8192:
+            grid = (n_rows,)
+            softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE)
+        else:
+            nb = self.nb
+            mid_max = self._mid_max[: n_rows * nb]
+            mid_sum = self._mid_sum[: n_rows * nb]
+            row_max = self._row_max[:n_rows]
+            row_sum = self._row_sum[:n_rows]
+            grid1 = (n_rows * nb,)
+            softmax_max_kernel[grid1](x, mid_max, mid_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=BLOCK_SIZE)
+            grid2 = (n_rows,)
+            softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](mid_max, mid_su

reasoning (3019 chars)
Great data! For each shape, the best BLOCK_SIZE is: - shape0 (32, 4096): 1024 or 2048 (0.0468). 2048 is same. - shape1 (16, 32768, nb=8): 2048 gives 0.0847, better than 1024 (0.0735). - shape2 (8, 131072, nb=16): 1024 gives 0.1662, best. 2048 is 0.1567. - shape3 (4, 262144, nb=32): 1024 gives 0.1685, best. 2048 is 0.1044. So we can use BLOCK_SIZE=2048 for shape1, and BLOCK_SIZE=1024 for shapes 2-4. For shape0, BLOCK_SIZE doesn't matter much. But can we use BLOCK_SIZE=2048 for the multi-block path in general? It hurts shapes 2-4. We need a shape-dependent BLOCK_SIZE. Since there are only 5 shapes, we can hardcode the best config per shape. But we also need the solution to be general. We can compute BLOCK_SIZE based on a heuristic. Looking at the data: - For small vocab (4096), BLOCK_SIZE=1024 is fine. - For vocab=32768, BLOCK_SIZE=2048 is best. - For vocab=131072 and 262144, BLOCK_SIZE=1024 is best. Why is 2048 worse for large vocab? Maybe because the block size compiled by Triton uses more registers or shared memory, reducing occupancy. For 1024, the compiler might use 128 threads with 8-wide vectorization. For 2048, it might use 256 threads or more registers per thread. The exact mapping is opaque. But we can simply use a dynamic BLOCK_SIZE: if `n_cols <= 32768`, use 2048; else use 1024. That would improve shape1 and not affect shape0. For other arbitrary shapes, 2048 for small, 1024 for large. Wait, shape1 is the only one that benefits from 2048. Let's check if BLOCK_SIZE=2048 helps shape0. It didn't (same as 1024). So we can just set BLOCK_SIZE=2048 for the multi-block path when `n_cols <= 65536`? But we need to ensure it doesn't hurt other shapes. Alternatively, we can set BLOCK_SIZE=2048 for the fused kernel, and for the multi-block path use BLOCK_SIZE=1024 except when `n_cols` is moderate. A simpler approach: use `BLOCK_SIZE = 1024` for all, but for shape1 specifically, we can increase `nb` to 16 and keep BLOCK_SIZE=1024. In the `test_nb_heuristic` test, for (16, 32768), nb=16 gave 0.0525 (worse). nb=8 gave 0.0844. With BLOCK_SIZE=2048 and nb=8, we get 0.0847. That's the best for shape1. What if we use nb=16 and BLOCK_SIZE=2048 for shape1? Let's test quickly. But before testing more, we can just hardcode a config table for the known shapes and fall back to a heuristic for unknown shapes. Since the benchmark only tests these 5 shapes, hardcoding is perfectly fine and robust. Let's do: ``` _CFG = { (32, 4096): {"fused": True, "block_size": 1024}, (16, 32768): {"fused": False, "nb": 8, "block_size": 2048}, (8, 131072): {"fused": False, "nb": 16, "block_size": 1024}, (4, 262144): {"fused": False, "nb": 32, "block_size": 1024}, } ``` In `__init__`, we can look up `(batch, vocab)` in `_CFG`. If found, use it. Otherwise, fall back to heuristic. But `__init__` only knows batch and vocab. It doesn't know about extreme flag. Shapes 2 and 4 have same (8, 131072), so same config. Let's test this exact config with `test_timing` style.

+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+class TestModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch, vocab, cfg):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.cfg = cfg
+        if not cfg.get("fused", False):
+            nb = cfg["nb"]
+            self._mid_max = torch.empty(batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._mid_sum = torch.empty(batch * nb, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._row_max = torch.empty(batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+            self._row_sum = torch.empty(batch, dtype=torch.float32, device="cuda")
+
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        cfg = self.cfg
+        if cfg.get("fused", False):
+            grid = (n_rows,)
+            softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=cfg["block_size"])
+        else:
+            nb = cfg["nb"]
+            bs = cfg["block_size"]
+            mid_max = self._mid_max[: n_rows * nb]
+            mid_sum = self._mid_sum[: n_rows * nb]
+            row_max = self._row_max[:n_rows]
+            row_sum = self._row_sum[:n_rows]
+            grid1 = (n_rows * nb,)
+            softmax_max_kernel[grid1](x, mid_max, mid_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=bs)
+            grid2 = (n_rows,)
+            softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, nb)
+            grid3 = (n_rows * nb,)
+            softmax_write_kernel[grid3](x, out, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=bs)
+        return out
+
+
+def _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme):
+    if e

Maybe we can process multiple rows per block to increase block occupancy. Earlier we tried `rows_per_block` but Triton didn't support `break`. We can avoid `break` by computing the exact number of rows per block and using a `while` loop or `for` loop with a fixed count and an `if` guard. Let's try a fused kernel where each block processes `ROWS_PER_BLOCK` rows. We can set `ROWS_PER_BLOCK` as a `tl.constexpr`. For shape0, batch=32. If we set `ROWS_PER_BLOCK=4`, we have 8 blocks. Each block processes 4 rows. That might reduce launch overhead and improve occupancy. Let's test. We need to avoid `break` in the Triton kernel. We can do: ``` block_idx = tl.program_id(0) row_start = block_idx * ROWS_PER_BLOCK for r in range(ROWS_PER_BLOCK): row_idx = row_start + r if row_idx < n_rows: ... process row ... ``` Triton supports `if` inside loops. It doesn't support `break`. So this is fine. Let's write a test with `ROWS_PER_BLOCK=4` for the fused kernel.

--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_rows.py
@@ -0,0 +1,107 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_rows_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    ROWS_PER_BLOCK: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    block_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_start = block_idx * ROWS_PER_BLOCK
+    if row_start >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    for r in range(ROWS_PER_BLOCK):
+        row_idx = row_start + r
+        if row_idx < n_rows:
+            row_in = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+            row_out = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+            row_max = -float('inf')
+            row_sum = 0.0
+            offset = 0
+            while offset < n_cols:
+                cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+                mask = cols < n_cols
+                x = tl.load(row_in + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+                block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+                block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+                new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+                scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+                scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+                row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+                row_max = new_max
+                offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+            offset = 0
+            while offset < n_cols:
+                cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+                mask = cols < n_cols
+                x = tl.load(row_in + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+                out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+                tl.store(row_out + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+                offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+class FusedRowsModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch, vocab, rows_per_block):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.rows_per_block = rows_per_block
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = ((n_rows + self.rows_per_block - 1) // self.rows_per_block,)
+        softmax_fused_rows_kernel[grid](
+            x, out, n_rows, n_cols,
+            ROWS_PER_BLOCK=self.rows_per_block,
+            BLOCK_SIZE=1024,
+        )
+        return out
+
+
+def _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme):
+    if extreme:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 2.0
+        idx = torch.randint(0, vocab, (batch, 4))
+        x.scatter_(1, idx, 30.0)
+    else:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 4.0
+    return x.to(torch.float32)
+
+
+def main():
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    shapes = [
+        (32, 4096, False),
+        (16, 32768, False),
+    ]
+    for batch, vocab, extreme in shapes:
+        torch.manual_seed(2026)
+        x = _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme).to(device)
+        print(f"\nbatch={batch} vocab={vocab}")
+        for rpb in [1, 2, 4, 8, 16]:
+            if rpb > batch:
+                continue
+            model = FusedRowsModel(batch, vocab, rpb).to(device).eval()
+            with torch.no_grad():
+                _ = model(x)
+            t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+            bytes_moved = batch * vocab * 8
+            gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+            peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+            print(f"  rpb={rpb:2d} ms={t:.4f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_bs_fused.py
@@ -0,0 +1,74 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+class Model(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=self.bs)
+        return out
+
+
+def main():
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    batch, vocab = 32, 4096
+    x = torch.randn(batch, vocab, dtype=torch.float32, device=device) * 4.0
+    print(f"batch={batch} vocab={vocab}")
+    for bs in [512, 1024, 2048, 4096]:
+        model = Model(bs).to(device).eval()
+        with torch.no_grad():
+            _ = model(x)
+        t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+        bytes_moved = batch * vocab * 8
+        gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+        peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+        print(f"  BLOCK_SIZE={bs:4d} ms={t:.4f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+# We will import the Model from solution.py after writing different configs.
+# Instead, we just copy the kernels here and test directly.
+
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr, mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+class FusedModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=self.bs)
+        return out
+
+
+class MultiModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, nb, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.nb = nb
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        nb = self.nb
+        bs = self.bs
+        mid_max = torch.empty(n_rows * nb, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        mid_sum = torch.empty(n_rows * nb, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        row_max = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        row_sum = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        grid1 = (n_rows * nb,)
+        softmax_max_kernel[grid1](x, mid_max, mid_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=bs)
+        grid2 = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, nb)
+        grid3 = (n_rows * nb,)
+        softmax_write_kernel[grid3](x, out, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=bs)
+        return out
+
+
+def _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme):
+    if extreme:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 2.0
+        id

+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr, mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr,

+):

+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block

+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)

+def _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme):
+    if extreme:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 2.0
+        idx = torch.randint(0, vocab, (batch, 4))
+        x.scatter_(1, idx, 30.0)
+    else:
+        x = torch.randn(batch, vocab) * 4.0
+    return x.to(torch.float32)

+def test_shape(batch, vocab, extreme, name, model):
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    torch.manual_seed(2026)
+    x = _make_inputs(batch, vocab, extreme).to(device)
+    with torch.no_grad():
+        _ = model(x)
+    import statistics
+    times = []
+    for _ in range(5):
+        t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+        times.append(t)
+    t = statistics.median(times)
+    bytes_moved = batch * vocab * 8
+    gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+    peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+    print(f"  {name:25s} ms={t:.4f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+

We also need to make sure the fallback for unknown shapes is sensible. Also, we should consider pre-allocating buffers for the multi-block path to avoid allocation overhead. In our isolated tests, we allocated inside `forward` each time. The benchmark's `time_fn` does 10 warmup + 30 timed calls. Allocation overhead might be amortized but could still add noise. In the previous solution.py, we pre-allocated in `__init__`. We should keep that. Let's write the final solution.py with pre-allocated buffers. One more thought: for shape1, fused with bs=4096 gave 0.1001 in isolation. In the actual benchmark, it might vary. But it's still much better than multi-block. Let's update solution.py and test.

If we can improve shape0 and shape1 further, the number goes up. For shape0, our isolated test showed fused_bs4096 at 0.0490, but benchmark gives 0.0373. That's a big discrepancy. Why? The benchmark time is 0.016 ms. Wait, isolated test gave 0.0119 ms. 0.016 ms is slower. The difference might be because the benchmark model is instantiated with `batch=32, vocab=4096` and buffers are pre-allocated? No, fused path doesn't allocate buffers. So it should be identical. Actually, in the benchmark, for shape0, the model is created with `init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()`. For shape0, `reference.BATCH = 32`, `reference.VOCAB = 4096`. `reference.get_init_inputs()` returns `[32, 4096]`. In our isolated test, it was 0.0119 ms. The benchmark does 10 warmup + 30 timed iterations with L2 flush. The isolated test also does 10 warmup + 30 timed iterations with L2 flush. The time of the L2 flush is not included, but maybe the GPU is still busy with the L2 flush when the kernel launches, causing the kernel to wait? `time_fn` does: ``` _l2_flush() torch.cuda.synchronize() s.record() fn(*inputs) e.record() torch.cuda.synchronize() ``` So it synchronizes after L2 flush before recording the start event. The kernel should not overlap with the flush. So that's fine. Let's run the benchmark a few more times to see the variance for shape0.

--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_shape0_multi.py
@@ -0,0 +1,186 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_max_kernel(
+    input_ptr, mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    mid_idx = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row + block_idx
+    local_max = -float('inf')
+    local_sum = 0.0
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(local_max, block_max)
+        scale_local = tl.exp(local_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        local_sum = local_sum * scale_local + block_sum * scale_block
+        local_max = new_max
+        offset += stride
+    tl.store(mid_max_ptr + mid_idx, local_max)
+    tl.store(mid_sum_ptr + mid_idx, local_sum)
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_reduce_kernel(
+    mid_max_ptr, mid_sum_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, num_blocks_per_row,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    base = row_idx * num_blocks_per_row
+    global_max = -float('inf')
+    global_sum = 0.0
+    for i in range(num_blocks_per_row):
+        m = tl.load(mid_max_ptr + base + i)
+        s = tl.load(mid_sum_ptr + base + i)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(global_max, m)
+        scale_global = tl.exp(global_max - new_max)
+        scale_m = tl.exp(m - new_max)
+        global_sum = global_sum * scale_global + s * scale_m
+        global_max = new_max
+    tl.store(row_max_ptr + row_idx, global_max)
+    tl.store(row_sum_ptr + row_idx, global_sum)
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_write_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, row_max_ptr, row_sum_ptr,
+    n_rows, n_cols, num_blocks_per_row, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    row_idx = pid // num_blocks_per_row
+    block_idx = pid % num_blocks_per_row
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = tl.load(row_max_ptr + row_idx)
+    row_sum = tl.load(row_sum_ptr + row_idx)
+    offset = block_idx * BLOCK_SIZE
+    stride = num_blocks_per_row * BLOCK_SIZE
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += stride
+
+
+class MultiModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, nb, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.nb = nb
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        nb = self.nb
+        bs = self.bs
+        mid_max = torch.empty(n_rows * nb, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        mid_sum = torch.empty(n_rows * nb, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        row_max = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        row_sum = torch.empty(n_rows, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device)
+        grid1 = (n_rows * nb,)
+        softmax_max_kernel[grid1](x, mid_max, mid_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=bs)
+        grid2 = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_reduce_kernel[grid2](mid_max, mid_sum, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, nb)
+        grid3 = (n_rows * nb,)
+        softmax_write_kernel[grid3](x, out, row_max, row_sum, n_rows, n_cols, nb, BLOCK_SIZE=bs)
+        return out
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+class FusedModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=self.bs)
+        return out
+
+

+        times.append(t)
+    t = statistics.median(times)
+    bytes_moved

Multi-block is terrible for shape0. Fused is clearly the best. The variance we see in benchmark is likely due to external factors (GPU clocks, background tasks). Since even the worst-case geomean is above 0.1, we are safe. However, we might try to improve shape0 by using a different approach: process multiple rows per block with fused kernel, but we saw that was bad. Or use vectorized loads? Triton does that automatically. What about using `torch.compile` on our Model? The benchmark compares against compiled reference, but we can't use `torch.compile` because it might fall back to library softmax (forbidden). But we can try `torch.compile` on our custom Model to see if it helps with launch overhead. However, `torch.compile` on a model that calls Triton kernels might not help much because the Triton kernel launch is already Python-level. `torch.compile` might fuse the Python overhead into a CUDA graph, which could eliminate launch overhead. That might improve small shapes significantly. But the user explicitly said: "This needs to be a real custom kernel. Don't import or call torch.nn.functional.softmax...". Using `torch.compile` on our custom kernel doesn't violate that rule. However, `torch.compile` might inline or rewrite our kernel calls. It might not be able to compile Triton kernels into a graph. Actually, `torch.compile` can compile Triton kernels if they are part of the FX graph. But the Triton kernel launch is a custom op (`triton.runtime.jit.JITFunction.__call__`). `torch.compile` might treat it as an opaque op and not graph it. In some cases, `torch.compile` can capture Triton kernels in CUDA graphs if they are deterministic. I'm not sure. Let's test `torch.compile` on our Model for shape0.

content (905 chars)
import sys
from pathlib import Path
REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))

import torch
from src.eval.timing import time_fn
from solution import Model

def main():
    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
    x = torch.randn(32, 4096, dtype=torch.float32, device=device) * 4.0
    model = Model(32, 4096).to(device).eval()
    comp = torch.compile(model, mode="reduce-overhead")

    # warmup
    with torch.no_grad():
        _ = comp(x)

    t = time_fn(comp, [x], iters=30)
    bytes_moved = 32 * 4096 * 8
    gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
    peak_frac = gbps / 1800
    print(f"compiled model ms={t:.4f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")

    t2 = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
    gbps2 = bytes_moved / (t2 / 1000) / 1e9
    peak_frac2 = gbps2 / 1800
    print(f"eager model  ms={t2:.4f} peak_frac={peak_frac2:.4f}")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

assistant
reasoning (3721 chars)
Now, let's think about further optimizations. One idea: for the fused kernel, we can reduce the number of reads from 2 to 1 by keeping the input in shared memory or registers between the online pass and the write pass. For small vocab (4096), a row is 16 KB. We can't keep 16 KB in registers, but we can keep it in shared memory. However, Triton abstracts shared memory; we can't explicitly allocate it. But we can load the entire row into a local tensor if BLOCK_SIZE >= n_cols. For n_cols=4096 and BLOCK_SIZE=4096, we load the whole row in one `tl.load`. Then we compute max and sum on that tensor. Then we can compute the output and write it without loading again. That would be 1 read + 1 write = 8 bytes/element. This would halve the HBM reads for the fused kernel. Wait, in our fused kernel, we do: ``` while offset < n_cols: x = tl.load(...) block_max = tl.max(x) block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max)) ... update row_max, row_sum ... offset += BLOCK_SIZE ``` Then a second while loop loads again. If n_cols <= BLOCK_SIZE, the first loop runs once. We have `x` loaded. But after the loop, `x` goes out of scope (or is overwritten). We can't reuse it because the second loop is separate. But if n_cols <= BLOCK_SIZE, we can load the entire row into `x`, compute max and sum, then compute output and write, all without a second load. Because the whole row fits in one block. For n_cols=4096 and BLOCK_SIZE=4096, we can do this. For n_cols=32768 and BLOCK_SIZE=4096, we can't fit the whole row in one block. But we could still reduce reads by storing loaded chunks in a global scratchpad and reading from it in the write pass. But that adds writes/reads, so no net gain. For shape0 (4096), a single-load kernel would read 16 KB and write 16 KB = 32 KB. At 1800 GB/s, that's 17.8 microseconds. Our current kernel takes ~12-16 microseconds. So we are already close to the memory bandwidth limit. The improvement from halving reads would be modest. But let's try to write a specialized fused kernel for `n_cols <= BLOCK_SIZE` that loads once. This might improve shape0. ``` @triton.jit def softmax_fused_oneshot_kernel(input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr): row_idx = tl.program_id(0) if row_idx >= n_rows: return row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols cols = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE) mask = cols < n_cols x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf')) row_max = tl.max(x, axis=0) row_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - row_max), axis=0) out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask) ``` This is extremely simple and should be very fast for small rows. For n_cols=4096, BLOCK_SIZE=4096, it loads once, computes max and sum, writes output. Total HBM traffic = 16 KB read + 16 KB write = 32 KB. At 1800 GB/s, time = 17.8 us. The kernel might be close to that. For shape0, this could be faster than the current two-pass fused kernel. Let's test it. For shape1 (32768), BLOCK_SIZE=4096 is not enough to cover the whole row. We could use a loop: load chunk, compute max, accumulate. But we need to write output after computing global sum. We could store chunks in a scratchpad. But that's extra memory traffic. Alternatively, we can use the online softmax approach but with a single loop that updates running max/sum and also writes to a temporary buffer. Then after the loop, we read the temporary buffer and divide. That's 1 read (input) + 1 write (temp) + 1 read (temp) + 1 write (output). That's 4 passes, worse. So the one-shot kernel only works for `n_cols <= BLOCK_SIZE`. Let's test the one-shot kernel for shape0.

+++ b//home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/04_kahan_softmax/test_oneshot.py
@@ -0,0 +1,120 @@
+import sys
+from pathlib import Path
+REPO_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
+sys.path.insert(0, str(REPO_ROOT))
+
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+from src.eval.timing import time_fn
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_oneshot_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+
+    cols = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+    mask = cols < n_cols
+    x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+    row_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+    row_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - row_max), axis=0)
+    out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+    tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+
+
+class OneShotModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_oneshot_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=self.bs)
+        return out
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def softmax_fused_kernel(
+    input_ptr, output_ptr, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    row_max = -float('inf')
+    row_sum = 0.0
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        block_max = tl.max(x, axis=0)
+        block_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - block_max), axis=0)
+        new_max = tl.maximum(row_max, block_max)
+        scale_row = tl.exp(row_max - new_max)
+        scale_block = tl.exp(block_max - new_max)
+        row_sum = row_sum * scale_row + block_sum * scale_block
+        row_max = new_max
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+    offset = 0
+    while offset < n_cols:
+        cols = offset + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)
+        mask = cols < n_cols
+        x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))
+        out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+        tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)
+        offset += BLOCK_SIZE
+
+
+class FusedModel(torch.nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, bs):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.bs = bs
+    def forward(self, x):
+        n_rows, n_cols = x.shape
+        out = torch.empty_like(x)
+        grid = (n_rows,)
+        softmax_fused_kernel[grid](x, out, n_rows, n_cols, BLOCK_SIZE=self.bs)
+        return out
+
+
+def test(name, model, x):
+    with torch.no_grad():
+        _ = model(x)
+    import statistics
+    times = []
+    for _ in range(5):
+        t = time_fn(model, [x], iters=30)
+        times.append(t)
+    t = statistics.median(times)
+    bytes_moved = 32 * 4096 * 8
+    gbps = bytes_moved / (t / 1000) / 1e9
+    peak_frac = gbps / 1800
+    print(f"{name:20s} ms={t:.4f} peak_frac={peak_frac:.4f}")
+
+
+def main():
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    x = torch.randn(32, 4096, dtype=torch.float32, device=device) * 4.0
+    print("shape0 (32, 4096)")
+    test("fused_bs1024", FusedModel(1024), x)
+    test("fused_bs2048", FusedModel(2048), x)
+    test("fused_bs4096", FusedModel(4096), x)
+    test("oneshot_bs4096", OneShotModel(4096), x)
+    test("oneshot_bs8192", OneShotModel(8192), x)
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

 @triton.jit
+def softmax_oneshot_kernel(
+    input_ptr,
+    output_ptr,
+    n_rows,
+    n_cols,
+    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """One-shot softmax for rows that fit in a single tile (n_cols <= BLOCK_SIZE).
+    Loads the row once, computes max & sum, and writes the output.
+    """
+    row_idx = tl.program_id(0)
+    if row_idx >= n_rows:
+        return
+
+    row_start = input_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+    out_start = output_ptr + row_idx * n_cols
+

+    mask = cols < n_cols
+    x = tl.load(row_start + cols, mask=mask, other=-float('inf'))

+    row_sum = tl.sum(tl.exp(x - row_max), axis=0)
+    out_val = tl.exp(x - row_max) / row_sum
+    tl.store(out_start + cols, out_val, mask=mask)

Oops, RESULT: LOW! Why did shape2 and shape4 drop? shape2 went from 0.170 to 0.1108, shape4 from 0.171 to 0.1116. That's a huge regression. But we didn't change the multi-block kernels or the config for those shapes. The only difference is we added the `softmax_oneshot_kernel` to the file, which changed line numbers, causing Triton to recompile the multi-block kernels. But the compiled code should be the same. Wait, maybe the issue is that we changed the order of kernels in the file, and Triton's JIT cache uses the file content as part of the cache key. If the cache is invalidated, the kernels are recompiled. But recompilation should produce identical code. However, there might be a subtle issue: Triton 3.6.0 has nondeterministic compilation behavior or autotuning heuristics that depend on the order in which kernels are compiled. For example, shared memory allocation or register allocation might differ based on the state of the compiler. This is unlikely but possible. Alternatively, the benchmark might have run during a period of GPU throttling. Let's run it again.
